     edit
     MediHelp — Remaining Phases Implementation Plan

     Context

     Phase 1 (Foundation) and Phase 2 backend (4 core services) are complete.
     All 9 Maven modules compile. We have 171 Java files, 63 REST endpoints, 22
     entities, 5 RabbitMQ listeners, and full Docker Compose infra. The backend
     is a finished product with no consumer — no frontend exists yet.

     Strategy: Build Angular frontend FIRST, then intelligence features.

     A clickable UI that a professor can demo is worth 10x more than invisible
     FHIR export endpoints. Phase 3 items (Resend email, OpenFDA, FHIR) are
     small single-file changes that can slot in later.

     ---
     Phase 2A — Angular Foundation (Next)

     Step 1: Scaffold Angular project

     cd medihelp-frontend
     npx @angular/cli@17 new medihelp-app --style=scss --routing --standalone
     --skip-git

     Install dependencies: @angular/material, @angular/cdk, ngx-charts (for
     vitals trends)

     Step 2: Core Infrastructure Files

     src/app/
       core/
         services/auth.service.ts       # login, register, verifyOtp, logout,
     refresh
         interceptors/auth.interceptor.ts  # Attaches Bearer token, handles
     401→login redirect
         guards/auth.guard.ts           # canActivate: token exists + not
     expired
         models/                        # TypeScript interfaces matching all
     backend DTOs
       features/
         auth/login/ register/          # Public routes
         dashboard/                     # Main page after login
         profile/                       # User profile CRUD
         vitals/                        # Record + view + trend charts
         prescriptions/                 # List + create + OCR upload
         medications/                   # Active meds + adherence logging
         appointments/                  # CRUD + upcoming view
         mood/                          # Mood entry + history
         notifications/                 # List + mark read + preferences
       shared/
         components/navbar/ sidebar/    # Layout components

     Key architectural rules:
     - All API calls go through gateway at http://localhost:8080 — never call
     services directly
     - Frontend only sends Authorization: Bearer <token> — gateway extracts
     X-User-Id from JWT
     - All responses wrapped in ApiResponse<T> — unwrap .data in every service
     method
     - Use standalone components (Angular 17+), no NgModules
     - Simple BehaviorSubject for shared state — no NgRx

     Step 3: Auth Pages

     - Login form → POST /api/v1/auth/login → store tokens in localStorage →
     redirect to /dashboard
     - Register form → POST /api/v1/auth/register → show OTP input → POST 
     /api/v1/auth/verify-otp → redirect to /login

     Step 4: Dashboard (the centerpiece)

     API calls on load:
     - GET /api/v1/health/vitals/latest → vital cards (HR, BP, weight, SpO2,
     temp)
     - GET /api/v1/health/score → circular health score gauge
     - GET /api/v1/health/streaks → streak flame icons
     - GET /api/v1/notifications/unread-count → badge on navbar bell
     - GET /api/v1/prescriptions/appointments/upcoming → upcoming appointments
     list

     Step 5: Feature Pages (parallelizable by team members)

     ┌───────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
     ┐
     │     Page      │                    API Endpoints Used
     │
     ├───────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
     ┤
     │ Vitals        │ POST /health/vitals, GET /health/vitals, GET
     │
     │               │ /health/vitals/trends
     │
     ├───────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
     ┤
     │ Prescriptions │ POST/GET /prescriptions, POST /ai/ocr/process, POST
     │
     │               │ /prescriptions/{id}/confirm-ocr
     │
     ├───────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
     ┤
     │ Medications   │ POST/GET /prescriptions/medications, POST
     │
     │               │ /medications/log, GET /medications/log/adherence
     │
     ├───────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
     ┤
     │ Appointments  │ POST/GET /prescriptions/appointments, GET
     │
     │               │ /appointments/upcoming, DELETE /{id}
     │
     ├───────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
     ┤
     │ Mood          │ POST/GET /health/mood
     │
     ├───────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
     ┤
     │ Profile       │ GET/PUT /users/me, CRUD /users/me/allergies,
     │
     │               │ /emergency-contacts, /conditions
     │
     ├───────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
     ┤
     │ Notifications │ GET /notifications, PATCH /{id}/read, PATCH /read-all,
     │
     │               │ GET/PUT /preferences
     │
     └───────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
     ┘

     Step 6: Frontend CI + Docker

     - Add build-angular job to .github/workflows/ci.yml
     - Create medihelp-frontend/Dockerfile (multi-stage: node:20-alpine →
     nginx:alpine)
     - Add frontend service to docker-compose.yml

     ---
     Phase 3 — Intelligence Layer (after frontend MVP)

     Small, self-contained backend changes:

     ┌─────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────────────┬───────┐
     │  Task   │                    File to Modify                     │ Effor │
     │         │                                                       │   t   │
     ├─────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────┼───────┤
     │ Resend  │ notification-service/.../service/EmailService.java    │ 1     │

     │ FHIR    │ New health-service/.../controller/FhirExportControlle │ 3     │
     │ export  │ r.java (HAPI FHIR dep already in pom)                 │ hours │
     ├─────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────┼───────┤
     │ Firebas │ notification-service/.../service/PushNotificationServ │ 4+    │
     │ e FCM   │ ice.java — SKIP unless time                           │ hours │
     └─────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────────────────┴───────┘

     Phase 4 — Deploy & Polish

     1. Oracle Cloud Free Tier — Docker Compose on ARM VM (4 OCPUs, 24GB RAM)
     2. Grafana Cloud — Alloy agent scraping /actuator/prometheus endpoints
     (already exposed)

     EmergencyContactController

     ---
     MVP vs Nice-to-Have

     MVP (must ship): Auth, Dashboard, Vitals, Medications, Appointments,
     Notifications, Profile, Docker deploy
     Nice-to-have: Mood journal, Family hub, OCR upload, FHIR export, Resend

❯ can we go for AWS cloud free tier instead of Oracle Cloud Free Tier?          

● Yes, but there's an important trade-off to know:

  ┌──────────────────┬──────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────┐
  │                  │      AWS Free Tier       │  Oracle Cloud Free Tier  │
  ├──────────────────┼──────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────┤
  │ Compute          │ t2.micro: 1 vCPU, 1GB    │ Ampere A1: 4 OCPUs, 24GB │
  │                  │ RAM                      │  RAM                     │
  ├──────────────────┼──────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────┤
  │ Duration         │ 12 months only           │ Forever free             │
  ├──────────────────┼──────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────┤
  │ RAM for 8        │ Not enough (need ~4GB)   │ Plenty                   │
  │ services         │                          │                          │
  ├──────────────────┼──────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────┤
  │ RDS PostgreSQL   │ 1 instance, 20GB, 12     │ Not included             │
  │                  │ months                   │                          │
  └──────────────────┴──────────────────────────┴──────────────────────────┘

  The problem: each Spring Boot service uses ~256-512MB RAM. With 7 Java
  services, you need ~3.5GB minimum. A t2.micro (1GB) can't run the full stack.

  But we can make it work. Here are the options:

● Everything is ready for Azure. Here's your step-by-step:

  ---
  Your Action Steps for Azure Deployment

  Step 1: Create Azure VM (10 min)

  1. Go to portal.azure.com → sign in with your student email
  2. Create a resource → Virtual Machine
  3. Settings:
    - Subscription: Azure for Students
    - Resource group: medihelp-rg (create new)
    - Name: medihelp-server
    - Image: Ubuntu Server 22.04 LTS
    - Size: Standard_B2s (2 vCPU, 4GB RAM, ~$30/month)
    - Auth: SSH public key
  4. Networking: Allow ports 22, 80, 8080
  5. Create → note the Public IP

  Step 2: Create free database accounts (15 min)

  ┌───────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │      Service      │                        Action                        │
  ├───────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ neon.tech         │ Create 5 projects (auth, user, health, prescription, │
  │                   │  notification)                                       │
  ├───────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ mongodb.com/atlas │ Create free M0 cluster, allow network from 0.0.0.0/0 │
  └───────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

  Step 3: Push code to GitHub first

  cd ~/medihelp
  git add -A
  git commit -m "MediHelp: Complete microservice health assistant"
  git branch -M main
  git remote add origin https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/medihelp.git
  git push -u origin main

  Step 4: SSH into Azure VM and deploy

  ssh azureuser@YOUR_VM_IP

  # Run setup script
  curl -sSL https://raw.githubusercontent.com/YOUR_USERNAME/medihelp/main/deploy
  /setup-azure-vm.sh | bash

  # Log out and back in
  exit
  ssh azureuser@YOUR_VM_IP

  # Edit .env with your Neon/Atlas/Gemini credentials
  nano ~/medihelp/.env

  # Clone, build, and deploy
  git clone https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/medihelp.git ~/medihelp-src
  cd ~/medihelp-src
  mvn clean package -DskipTests -B
  cd medihelp-frontend && npm ci && npx ng build && cd ..
  docker compose -f docker-compose.prod.yml build
  cp docker-compose.prod.yml ~/medihelp/docker-compose.yml
  cd ~/medihelp
  docker compose up -d

  Step 5: Save credits — stop VM when not using it

  az vm deallocate --resource-group medihelp-rg --name medihelp-server  # Stop 
  billing
  az vm start --resource-group medihelp-rg --name medihelp-server       # Resume

  Key files created/updated:
  - deploy/setup-azure-vm.sh — automated VM setup script
  - deploy/DEPLOYMENT.md — full deployment guide
  - docker-compose.prod.yml — with JVM memory limits for 4GB VM
  - All Dockerfiles — now support JAVA_OPTS environment variable
  - .github/workflows/deploy.yml — works with any VM (Azure/Oracle)

  Want me to help with any of these steps?

● I can see the issue — the selected size Standard_D2s_v3 ($70/month) is
  unavailable for your student subscription in East US, and it's also too
  expensive.

  Here's what to change:

  Fix these settings:

  1. Size — Click "See all sizes" and search for:
    - Standard_B2s (2 vCPU, 4GB, ~$30/month) — best option
    - If B2s is also unavailable, try Standard_B1ms (1 vCPU, 2GB, ~$15/month) —
  tighter but works with swap
    - Or Standard_B2ls_v2 if listed — cheaper B-series
  2. Region — If B2s shows unavailable in East US too, try changing to:
    - East US 2
    - West US 2
    - Central India
    - North Europe
  3. Everything else looks good — Ubuntu 24.04, x64, SSH key, no spot discount

  The B-series trick

  Azure for Students often restricts D-series (compute-optimized) VMs. B-series 
  (burstable) VMs are what student subscriptions are designed for — they're
  cheaper and almost always available.

  Steps:

  1. Click "See all sizes"
  2. In the search/filter box type B2s
  3. Select it
  4. If grayed out → change Region dropdown and try again

  Let me know what sizes show as available and I'll help you pick the best one.

      azureuser@98.70.34.96 "echo 'Connected!' && uname -a && free -h | head -3"
       2>&1)
  ⎿  Error: Exit code 255
     Warning: Permanently added '98.70.34.96' (ED25519) to the list of known 
     hosts.


● I can't SSH from here — I don't have your private key (.pem file). You'll need
   to run the setup commands yourself.

  First, open port 8080 on the VM (we need this for the Gateway):

  1. In Azure Portal → go to your VM → Networking → Network settings
  2. Click Create port rule → Inbound port rule
  3. Destination port: 8080, Protocol: TCP, Name: AllowGateway, Priority: 310
  4. Add

  Then SSH in from your local terminal and run these commands:

  # 1. SSH into VM (use the path where you saved the .pem file)
  chmod 400 ~/Downloads/medihelp-server_key.pem
  ssh -i ~/Downloads/medihelp-server_key.pem azureuser@98.70.34.96

  # 2. Install Docker + JDK + Node.js + create swap (copy-paste this entire 
  block)
  sudo apt update && sudo apt upgrade -y && \
  sudo apt install -y ca-certificates curl gnupg && \
  sudo install -m 0755 -d /etc/apt/keyrings && \
  curl -fsSL https://download.docker.com/linux/ubuntu/gpg | sudo gpg --dearmor
  -o /etc/apt/keyrings/docker.gpg && \
  sudo chmod a+r /etc/apt/keyrings/docker.gpg && \
  echo "deb [arch=$(dpkg --print-architecture) 
  signed-by=/etc/apt/keyrings/docker.gpg] 
  https://download.docker.com/linux/ubuntu $(. /etc/os-release && echo 
  "$VERSION_CODENAME") stable" | sudo tee /etc/apt/sources.list.d/docker.list >
  /dev/null && \
  sudo apt update && \
  sudo apt install -y docker-ce docker-ce-cli containerd.io
  docker-compose-plugin openjdk-21-jdk-headless maven git && \
  curl -fsSL https://deb.nodesource.com/setup_20.x | sudo -E bash - && \
  sudo apt install -y nodejs && \
  sudo systemctl enable docker && \
  sudo usermod -aG docker $USER && \
  sudo fallocate -l 4G /swapfile && sudo chmod 600 /swapfile && \
  sudo mkswap /swapfile && sudo swapon /swapfile && \
  echo '/swapfile none swap sw 0 0' | sudo tee -a /etc/fstab && \
  echo "SETUP COMPLETE - now log out and back in"

  # 3. Log out and back in (for Docker group)
  exit
  ssh -i ~/Downloads/medihelp-server_key.pem azureuser@98.70.34.96

  # 4. Verify
  docker --version && java --version && node --version && echo "All good!"

  Run these and let me know when you see "All good!" — I'll give you the next
  steps (clone repo, build, deploy).

  sudo apt update && sudo apt upgrade -y && \
  sudo apt install -y ca-certificates curl gnupg && \
  sudo install -m 0755 -d /etc/apt/keyrings && \
  curl -fsSL https://download.docker.com/linux/ubuntu/gpg | sudo gpg --dearmor
  -o /etc/apt/keyrings/docker.gpg && \

  signed-by=/etc/apt/keyrings/docker.gpg]

  "$VERSION_CODENAME") stable" | sudo tee /etc/apt/sources.list.d/docker.list >
  /dev/null && \

  docker-compose-plugin openjdk-21-jdk-headless maven git && \
  curl -fsSL https://deb.nodesource.com/setup_20.x | sudo -E bash - && \
  sudo apt install -y nodejs && \
  sudo systemctl enable docker && \
  sudo usermod -aG docker $USER && \
  sudo fallocate -l 4G /swapfile && sudo chmod 600 /swapfile && \
  sudo mkswap /swapfile && sudo swapon /swapfile && \
  echo '/swapfile none swap sw 0 0' | sudo tee -a /etc/fstab && \
  echo "===== SETUP COMPLETE ====="

  Replace YOUR_USERNAME with your GitHub username. If the repo doesn't exist

  2. Create Neon databases (neon.tech)

  Sign up and create 5 projects:
  - medihelp-auth
  - medihelp-user
  - medihelp-health
  - medihelp-prescription
  - medihelp-notification

  For each, copy the connection string from the dashboard. It looks like:
  postgresql://neondb_owner:password@ep-something.region.aws.neon.tech/neondb

  3. Create MongoDB Atlas cluster (mongodb.com/atlas)

  - Create free M0 cluster
  - Database user: medihelp / choose a password
  - Network access: Allow from anywhere (0.0.0.0/0)
  - Copy connection string:
  mongodb+srv://medihelp:pass@cluster.mongodb.net/medihelp_health

● STOP — you accidentally committed your SSH private key! That's a security
  risk. Let me fix this first.

  Run these in your WSL terminal:

  cd ~/medihelp
  git rm --cached medihelp-server_key.pem
  medihelp-server_key.pem:Zone.Identifier azure-portal-settings.png
  echo "medihelp-server_key.pem" >> .gitignore
  echo "*.pem" >> .gitignore
  echo "*.Zone.Identifier" >> .gitignore
  echo "*.png" >> .gitignore
  git add .gitignore
  git commit -m "Remove accidentally committed private key and screenshots"

  Then push:

  git push -u origin main

  Move the .pem file out of the project directory to somewhere safe:

  mv ~/medihelp/medihelp-server_key.pem ~/medihelp-server_key.pem

  Let me know once the push succeeds. Then we'll clone on the Azure VM and
  deploy.

● Yes! Since the app is deployed on Azure cloud (not inside your WSL), you can
  access it from any browser on any device:

  - Frontend: http://98.70.34.96
  - Eureka Dashboard: http://98.70.34.96:8761

  Try it right now — open http://98.70.34.96 in Chrome/Edge on your Windows
  machine.

  The Angular frontend will call the Gateway at http://98.70.34.96:8080 for all
  API requests. But wait — there's one thing to check. The frontend's
  environment config might be set to localhost:8080. Let me verify.

  Read 2 files (ctrl+o to expand)

● The production build uses apiUrl: '' (empty string) — meaning API calls will
  go to the same host the frontend is served from (port 80). But the Gateway is
  on port 8080. We need to fix this. Two options — easiest is to configure Nginx
   to proxy /api requests to the Gateway.

  Run these on the Azure VM:

  sudo tee /etc/nginx/sites-available/default << 'EOF'
  server {
      listen 80;
      server_name _;
      root /var/www/html;
      index index.html;

      location / {
          try_files $uri $uri/ /index.html;
      }

      location /api/ {
          proxy_pass http://localhost:8080;
          proxy_set_header Host $host;
          proxy_set_header X-Real-IP $remote_addr;
      }

      location /actuator/ {
          proxy_pass http://localhost:8080;
      }
  }
  EOF

  Then:

  sudo nginx -t && sudo systemctl restart nginx

  After that, open http://98.70.34.96 in your Windows browser — the frontend
  will load and API calls will route through Nginx to the Gateway. Try
  registering a user!

❯ azureuser@medihelp-server:~/medihelp-src$ sudo tee                            
/etc/nginx/sites-available/default << 'EOF'                                     
  server {                                                                      
      listen 80;                                                                
      server_name _;                                                            
      root /var/www/html;                                                       
      index index.html;                                                         
                                                                                
      location / {                                                              
          try_files $uri $uri/ /index.html;                                     
      }                                                                         
                                                                                
      location /api/ {                                                          
          proxy_pass http://localhost:8080;                                     
          proxy_set_header Host $host;                                          
          proxy_set_header X-Real-IP $remote_addr;                              
      }                                                                         
                                                                                
      location /actuator/ {                                                     
          proxy_pass http://localhost:8080;                                     
      }                                                                         
  }                                                                             
  EOF

● The API works fine via curl — no errors. The issue is likely CORS. The browser
   is blocking the frontend (port 80) from calling the Gateway (port 8080). But
  since we set up Nginx to proxy /api/ requests, the frontend shouldn't be
  calling port 8080 directly.

  Let me check the Angular service to see how it makes API calls.

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● The apiUrl is empty string in production (environment.prod.ts), so it calls
  /api/v1/auth/register — which Nginx proxies to the Gateway. That should work.

  The issue is likely in the register component — it may be catching the error
  wrong, or the response mapping fails because register returns res.data which
  is null (the response has success and message but no data field).

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● Found it. The authService.register() does map(res => res.data) but the
  register endpoint returns {"success": true, "message": "...", "timestamp": 
  "..."} with no data field. When res.data is undefined, the RxJS pipeline may
  throw, triggering the error handler.

  The fix is simple — the register method should map the full response, not just
   data. But since the frontend is already built and deployed on the VM, the
  fastest fix is to rebuild on the VM. Let me fix it locally first.

● Update(medihelp-frontend/src/app/core/services/auth.service.ts)
  ⎿  File must be read first

● The file was already read above. Let me try the path exactly:

● Bash(cd /home/subhra28/medihelp/medihelp-frontend/src/app/core/services && sed
       -i "s/map(res => res.data)/map(res => res)/g" auth.service.ts && echo
      "Fixed")
  ⎿  Fixed

● That changed ALL map calls including login. Let me fix login back to use
  res.data:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● Login and refresh need res.data back since they return an AuthResponse object.
   Let me fix precisely:

● Update(medihelp-frontend/src/app/core/services/auth.service.ts)
  ⎿  Added 1 line, removed 1 line

● Nginx isn't proxying /api/ requests. The config didn't save properly earlier.
  Fix it:

  sudo nano /etc/nginx/sites-available/default

  Delete everything in the file (Ctrl+K repeatedly), then paste this:

  server {
      listen 80;
      server_name _;
      root /var/www/html;
      index index.html;

      location / {
          try_files $uri $uri/ /index.html;
      }

      location /api/ {
          proxy_pass http://localhost:8080;
          proxy_set_header Host $host;
          proxy_set_header X-Real-IP $remote_addr;
      }
  }

  Save with Ctrl+O, Enter, Ctrl+X. Then:

  sudo nginx -t

  sudo systemctl restart nginx

  Then test:

      6 echo ""

       10 +## Features                                                   
       11 +                                                              
       12 +- **AI Symptom Triage** - Describe symptoms in plain language,
          + get urgency classification via Google Gemini                 
       13 +- **Prescription OCR** - Upload prescription images, extract m
          +edication details via Tesseract                               
       14 +- **Vitals Tracking** - Record and monitor heart rate, blood p
          +ressure, temperature, SpO2, blood sugar                       
       15 +- **Anomaly Detection** - Real-time alerts when vitals exceed 
          +thresholds (Welford's algorithm)                              
       16 +- **Medication Management** - Track medications, auto-schedule
          + reminders, log adherence                                     
       17 +- **Health Score Gamification** - 0-100 score with streaks and
          + badges                                                       
       18 +- **FHIR R4 Export** - Export health data in industry-standard
          + FHIR format with LOINC codes                                 
       19 +- **Mood Journaling** - Daily mood tracking with sleep/exercis
          +e correlation                                                 
       20 +- **Family Health Hub** - Manage dependents with role-based ac
          +cess (Owner/Caregiver/Viewer)                                 
       21 +- **Emergency SOS** - One-tap alert sends medical summary to e
          +mergency contacts                                             
       22 +- **Drug Interaction Checker** - OpenFDA-powered interaction c
          +hecking with local cache                                      
       23 +- **Smart Notifications** - RabbitMQ event-driven notification
          +s for reminders, alerts, appointments

● The .ps1 scripts are for Windows PowerShell, not Linux. To stop the Azure VM,
  you have two options:

  Option A: From WSL (install Azure CLI first)

  curl -sL https://aka.ms/InstallAzureCLIDeb | sudo bash

  Then login and stop:
  az login
  az vm deallocate --resource-group medihelp-rg --name medihelp-server

  Option B: From Windows PowerShell (open a regular PowerShell window, not WSL)

  az vm deallocate --resource-group medihelp-rg --name medihelp-server

  Option C: Just use the Azure Portal

  Go to portal.azure.com → Virtual Machines → medihelp-server → click Stop.

  This is the simplest option. Use the portal to stop/start the VM whenever you
  want to save credits.

  To start it again later: same portal page → click Start.

● PowerShell blocks scripts by default. Quick fix — just run the command
  directly in PowerShell:

  az vm deallocate --resource-group medihelp-rg --name medihelp-server

  That's it. No script needed. When you want to start it again:

  az vm start --resource-group medihelp-rg --name medihelp-server

  If az is not installed on Windows, just use the Azure Portal — it's two
  clicks: portal.azure.com → Virtual Machines → medihelp-server → Stop / Start.

● Now I have the complete picture. Here's the comprehensive summary:

  ---
  COMPLETE PROJECT SUMMARY

  What is MediHelp?

  A personalised health assistant web app with 9 microservices that provides
  pre-diagnosis support (AI symptom triage), post-appointment monitoring
  (medication tracking, adherence), and continuous health management (vitals,
  mood, diet) — built as a college group project (3-4 members) using free
  student resources.

  What's Built (by file count)

  183 Java + 11 Python + 58 Angular + 28 Config + 9 Docker + 10 Scripts = ~299
  files
  70 REST endpoints | 22 JPA entities | 1 MongoDB document | 7 RabbitMQ events |
   6 listeners

  The 9 Microservices — All Working

  Service: Eureka
  Port: 8761
  What it does: Service discovery
  Files: 1 Java
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Service: API Gateway
  Port: 8080
  What it does: JWT validation, routing, rate limiting (Redis), CORS
  Files: 4 Java
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Service: Auth
  Port: 8081
  What it does: Register, OTP verify, login (JWT), refresh, logout (Redis
    blacklist), forgot/reset password
  Files: 18 Java
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Service: User Profile
  Port: 8082
  What it does: Profiles, family hub (OWNER/CAREGIVER/VIEWER), emergency
    contacts, allergies, conditions, Emergency SOS with GPS +  shareable links
  Files: 41 Java
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Service: Health Tracking
  Port: 8083
  What it does: Vitals CRUD, Welford's anomaly detection, mood journal (AES-256 
    encrypted, MongoDB), health score (0-100), streaks (with freeze),  badges,
    FHIR R4 export (LOINC codes)
  Files: 37 Java
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Service: Prescription
  Port: 8084
  What it does: Prescriptions, medications (auto-scheduling), adherence logs
    (TAKEN/MISSED/SKIPPED), appointments, drug interaction checker  (OpenFDA 
    API), scheduled reminders
  Files: 41 Java
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Service: AI Service
  Port: 8000
  What it does: Gemini symptom triage, Tesseract prescription OCR (OpenCV
    preprocessing), diet/exercise recommendations
  Files: 11 Python
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Service: Notification
  Port: 8085
  What it does: In-app notifications, preferences (quiet hours), RabbitMQ
    consumers (welcome, meds, anomaly, appointments, SOS), Resend  email API
  Files: 21 Java
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Service: Angular Frontend
  Port: 80
  What it does: Landing page, login/register (OTP), dashboard (health score,
    vitals, streaks), vitals, medications, appointments, profile, notifications
  Files: 58 files

  Where Are Specific Features?

  Feature: Gemini AI
  Where: medihelp-ai-service/app/services/gemini_service.py
  File: Uses gemini-1.5-flash, falls back to mock if no API key
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Feature: Prescription OCR
  Where: medihelp-ai-service/app/services/ocr_service.py + app/routers/ocr.py
  File: Tesseract + OpenCV preprocessing, endpoint: POST /api/v1/ai/ocr/process
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Feature: Symptom Triage
  Where: medihelp-ai-service/app/routers/symptoms.py
  File: POST /api/v1/ai/symptoms/triage
  ────────────────────────────────────────

  File: GET /api/v1/health/fhir/export
  ────────────────────────────────────────

  File: Welford's algorithm + threshold checks
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Feature: Drug Interactions

  File: OpenFDA API + local cache
  ────────────────────────────────────────

  Current Deployment Status

  Azure VM (98.70.34.96) — B2as_v2, 8GB RAM, Central India
  ├── Nginx (port 80) → Angular SPA
  ├── 7 Java services (ports 8080-8085, 8761) — running as background processes
  ├── Docker containers (local):
  │   ├── PostgreSQL x5 (auth, user, health, prescription, notification)
  │   ├── MongoDB (mood journals)
  │   ├── Redis (JWT blacklist, rate limiting)
  │   └── RabbitMQ (event bus)
  └── Auto-restart on boot (systemd enabled)

  Problem: All databases are local Docker on the VM. If the VM is deallocated,
  Docker volumes persist but data could be lost if the VM is deleted. The
  original plan was to use cloud-managed free databases.

  Now we need to update each service's application.yml on the VM to read from
  these env vars instead of local Docker. But actually, they already do — the
  application.yml files use ${DB_URL:jdbc:postgresql://localhost:...} format. We
   just need to export these env vars before starting services.

  Update the start script to load .env:

  cd ~/medihelp-src && head -1 deploy/scripts/start-all.sh

  Then add this line at the top of the start script (after the cd line):

  sed -i '/^cd "\$PROJECT_DIR"/a\\n# Load environment variables\nif [ -f 
  "$PROJECT_DIR/.env" ]; then\n  set -a\n  source "$PROJECT_DIR/.env"\n  set 
  +a\n  echo "  Loaded .env with cloud credentials"\nfi'
  deploy/scripts/start-all.sh

  Or simpler — just source the .env and restart:

  cd ~/medihelp-src && set -a && source .env && set +a && echo "Env loaded: 
  GEMINI=$GEMINI_API_KEY RESEND=$RESEND_API_KEY" | cut -c1-60

  Then restart all services with cloud databases:

  bash deploy/scripts/stop-all.sh

  cd ~/medihelp-src && set -a && source .env && set +a && bash
  deploy/scripts/start-all.sh

● So the services ARE using local Docker, not Neon. The ${DB_URL:...} syntax in
  the YAML is reading the default value because something about how the env var
  is passed isn't working with Spring's placeholder resolution.

  The definitive fix: override using Spring Boot's env var naming convention.
  Spring Boot auto-maps SPRING_DATASOURCE_URL to spring.datasource.url. This
  ALWAYS works.

  Step 1: Start local postgres back

  docker start medihelp-postgres-auth

  Step 2: Add Spring-native env vars to .env

  cat >> ~/medihelp-src/.env << 'EOF'
  SPRING_DATASOURCE_URL_AUTH=jdbc:postgresql://ep-falling-star-a1advi2d-pooler.a
  p-southeast-1.aws.neon.tech/neondb?sslmode=require
  SPRING_DATASOURCE_URL_USER=jdbc:postgresql://ep-noisy-bonus-a1yyoo4q-pooler.ap
  -southeast-1.aws.neon.tech/neondb?sslmode=require
  SPRING_DATASOURCE_URL_HEALTH=jdbc:postgresql://ep-autumn-breeze-a1ns6egq-poole
  r.ap-southeast-1.aws.neon.tech/neondb?sslmode=require
  SPRING_DATASOURCE_URL_PRESCRIPTION=jdbc:postgresql://ep-spring-breeze-a1pwwmwj
  -pooler.ap-southeast-1.aws.neon.tech/neondb?sslmode=require
  SPRING_DATASOURCE_URL_NOTIFICATION=jdbc:postgresql://ep-restless-queen-a18wf9x

  Actually, the issue is simpler. Each service reads ${DB_URL:default} but they
  ALL read the same env var DB_URL. We set AUTH_DB_URL, USER_DB_URL etc — but
  the YAML says ${DB_URL:...} not ${AUTH_DB_URL:...}.

● Found it! The YAML uses ${DB_URL:...} but our .env has AUTH_DB_URL,
  USER_DB_URL etc. They don't match. All services read the same DB_URL env var.

  The fix: each service needs its own env var OR we update the start script to
  set DB_URL differently for each service. The cleanest approach — update the
  start script to set DB_URL per service:

  cat > ~/medihelp-src/deploy/scripts/start-all.sh << 'SCRIPTEOF'
  #!/bin/bash
  PROJECT_DIR="${1:-$(dirname $(dirname $(dirname $(realpath $0))))}"
  cd "$PROJECT_DIR" || exit 1

  # Load cloud credentials
  set -a; source "$PROJECT_DIR/.env" 2>/dev/null; set +a

  echo "========================================="
  echo "  MediHelp - Starting All Services"
  echo "========================================="

  echo "[1/4] Starting infrastructure..."
  docker compose -f docker-compose.infra.yml up -d 2>/dev/null
  sleep 5
  echo "  Waiting for infrastructure to be healthy..."
  for i in {1..30}; do
      healthy=$(docker ps --filter "health=healthy" --format "{{.Names}}"
  2>/dev/null | wc -l)
      total=$(docker ps --format "{{.Names}}" 2>/dev/null | wc -l)
      if [ "$healthy" -ge "$total" ] && [ "$total" -gt 0 ]; then
          echo "  All $total containers healthy."
          break
      fi
      sleep 2
  done

  echo "[2/4] Starting Eureka (service discovery)..."
  java -Xmx192m -jar medihelp-eureka/target/medihelp-eureka-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar
  &> /tmp/eureka.log &
  echo "  PID: $!"
  echo "  Waiting for Eureka..."
  for i in {1..40}; do
      if curl -s http://localhost:8761/actuator/health | grep -q "UP"
  2>/dev/null; then
          echo "  Eureka is UP."
          break
      fi
      sleep 2
  done

  echo "[3/4] Starting Gateway + microservices..."

  java -Xmx192m -jar medihelp-gateway/target/medihelp-gateway-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar
   &> /tmp/gateway.log &
  echo "  Gateway PID: $!"

  DB_URL="$AUTH_DB_URL" DB_USER="$AUTH_DB_USER" DB_PASSWORD="$AUTH_DB_PASSWORD"
  \
    java -Xmx256m -jar
  medihelp-auth-service/target/medihelp-auth-service-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar &>
  /tmp/auth.log &
  echo "  Auth PID: $!"

  DB_URL="$USER_DB_URL" DB_USER="$USER_DB_USER" DB_PASSWORD="$USER_DB_PASSWORD"
  \
    java -Xmx256m -jar
  medihelp-user-service/target/medihelp-user-service-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar &>
  /tmp/user.log &
  echo "  User PID: $!"

  DB_URL="$HEALTH_DB_URL" DB_USER="$HEALTH_DB_USER"
  DB_PASSWORD="$HEALTH_DB_PASSWORD" \
    java -Xmx256m -jar
  medihelp-health-service/target/medihelp-health-service-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar &>
  /tmp/health.log &
  echo "  Health PID: $!"

  DB_URL="$PRESCRIPTION_DB_URL" DB_USER="$PRESCRIPTION_DB_USER"
  DB_PASSWORD="$PRESCRIPTION_DB_PASSWORD" \
    java -Xmx256m -jar medihelp-prescription-service/target/medihelp-prescriptio
  n-service-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar &> /tmp/prescription.log &
  echo "  Prescription PID: $!"

  DB_URL="$NOTIFICATION_DB_URL" DB_USER="$NOTIFICATION_DB_USER"
  DB_PASSWORD="$NOTIFICATION_DB_PASSWORD" \
    java -Xmx256m -jar medihelp-notification-service/target/medihelp-notificatio
  n-service-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar &> /tmp/notification.log &
  echo "  Notification PID: $!"

  echo "[4/4] Waiting for services to start (50s)..."
  sleep 50

  echo ""
  echo "========================================="
  echo "  Service Health Check"
  echo "========================================="
  declare -A services=([8761]="Eureka" [8080]="Gateway" [8081]="Auth"
  [8082]="User" [8083]="Health" [8084]="Prescription" [8085]="Notification")
  all_up=true
  for port in 8761 8080 8081 8082 8083 8084 8085; do
      status=$(curl -s -o /dev/null -w "%{http_code}"
  http://localhost:$port/actuator/health 2>/dev/null)
      name=${services[$port]}
      if [ "$status" = "200" ]; then
          echo "  ✓ $name ($port): UP"
      else
          echo "  ✗ $name ($port): DOWN (HTTP $status)"
          all_up=false
      fi
  done
  echo ""
  if $all_up; then
      echo "All services are UP! MediHelp is ready."
  else
      echo "Some services still starting. Wait 30s and run: bash 
  deploy/scripts/status.sh"
  fi
  SCRIPTEOF
  chmod +x ~/medihelp-src/deploy/scripts/start-all.sh
  echo "Start script updated"

  Now restart:

  bash ~/medihelp-src/deploy/scripts/stop-all.sh

● Found it! The DB_URL="..." java -jar ... syntax broke because java isn't on
  the PATH in that context. The env var prefix syntax interfered. Let me fix the
   start script differently — export the vars before each java command instead:

  cat > ~/medihelp-src/deploy/scripts/start-all.sh << 'SCRIPTEOF'
  #!/bin/bash
  PROJECT_DIR="${1:-$(dirname $(dirname $(dirname $(realpath $0))))}"
  cd "$PROJECT_DIR" || exit 1

  # Load cloud credentials
  set -a; source "$PROJECT_DIR/.env" 2>/dev/null; set +a

  # Ensure java is on PATH
  export PATH="$PATH:/usr/lib/jvm/java-21-openjdk-amd64/bin:/usr/bin"
  export NVM_DIR="$HOME/.nvm"
  [ -s "$NVM_DIR/nvm.sh" ] && . "$NVM_DIR/nvm.sh"

  echo "========================================="
  echo "  MediHelp - Starting All Services"
  echo "========================================="

  echo "[1/4] Starting infrastructure..."
  docker compose -f docker-compose.infra.yml up -d 2>/dev/null
  sleep 5
  echo "  Infrastructure started."

  echo "[2/4] Starting Eureka (service discovery)..."
  java -Xmx192m -jar medihelp-eureka/target/medihelp-eureka-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar
  &> /tmp/eureka.log &

  echo "  Waiting for Eureka..."
  for i in {1..40}; do
      if curl -s http://localhost:8761/actuator/health | grep -q "UP"
  2>/dev/null; then
          echo "  Eureka is UP."
          break
      fi
      sleep 2
  done

  echo "[3/4] Starting Gateway + microservices..."

  java -Xmx192m -jar medihelp-gateway/target/medihelp-gateway-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar
   &> /tmp/gateway.log &
  echo "  Gateway PID: $!"

  export DB_URL="$AUTH_DB_URL" DB_USER="$AUTH_DB_USER"
  DB_PASSWORD="$AUTH_DB_PASSWORD"
  java -Xmx256m -jar
  medihelp-auth-service/target/medihelp-auth-service-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar &>
  /tmp/auth.log &
  echo "  Auth PID: $!"

  DB_PASSWORD="$USER_DB_PASSWORD"

  chmod +x ~/medihelp-src/deploy/scripts/start-all.sh
  echo "Script fixed"

  Wait — there's a problem with the export approach too. When you export DB_URL
  and then start background processes, all subsequent services get the LAST
  exported DB_URL. Background & processes inherit env at launch time, but export
   changes the global env.

  Better approach — use per-process env inline but with full java path:

  JAVA_CMD=$(which java)
  cat > ~/medihelp-src/deploy/scripts/start-all.sh << SCRIPTEOF
  #!/bin/bash
  PROJECT_DIR="\${1:-\$(dirname \$(dirname \$(dirname \$(realpath \$0))))}"
  cd "\$PROJECT_DIR" || exit 1

  set -a; source "\$PROJECT_DIR/.env" 2>/dev/null; set +a

  JAVA="$JAVA_CMD"

  echo "========================================="
  echo "  MediHelp - Starting All Services"
  echo "========================================="

  echo "[1/4] Starting infrastructure..."
  docker compose -f docker-compose.infra.yml up -d 2>/dev/null
  sleep 5
  echo "  Infrastructure started."

  echo "[2/4] Starting Eureka..."
  \$JAVA -Xmx192m -jar medihelp-eureka/target/medihelp-eureka-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar
   &> /tmp/eureka.log &
  echo "  PID: \$!"
  for i in {1..40}; do curl -s http://localhost:8761/actuator/health | grep -q 
  "UP" 2>/dev/null && echo "  Eureka is UP." && break; sleep 2; done

  echo "[3/4] Starting services..."

  \$JAVA -Xmx192m -jar 
  medihelp-gateway/target/medihelp-gateway-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar &> 
  /tmp/gateway.log &
  echo "  Gateway PID: \$!"

  DB_URL="\$AUTH_DB_URL" DB_USER="\$AUTH_DB_USER" 
  DB_PASSWORD="\$AUTH_DB_PASSWORD" \$JAVA -Xmx256m -jar 
  medihelp-auth-service/target/medihelp-auth-service-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar &> 
  /tmp/auth.log &
  echo "  Auth PID: \$!"

  DB_URL="\$USER_DB_URL" DB_USER="\$USER_DB_USER" 
  DB_PASSWORD="\$USER_DB_PASSWORD" \$JAVA -Xmx256m -jar 
  medihelp-user-service/target/medihelp-user-service-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar &> 
  /tmp/user.log &
  echo "  User PID: \$!"

  DB_URL="\$HEALTH_DB_URL" DB_USER="\$HEALTH_DB_USER" 
  DB_PASSWORD="\$HEALTH_DB_PASSWORD" \$JAVA -Xmx256m -jar 
  medihelp-health-service/target/medihelp-health-service-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar &> 
  /tmp/health.log &
  echo "  Health PID: \$!"

  DB_URL="\$PRESCRIPTION_DB_URL" DB_USER="\$PRESCRIPTION_DB_USER" 
  DB_PASSWORD="\$PRESCRIPTION_DB_PASSWORD" \$JAVA -Xmx256m -jar medihelp-prescri
  ption-service/target/medihelp-prescription-service-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar &> 
  /tmp/prescription.log &
  echo "  Prescription PID: \$!"

  DB_URL="\$NOTIFICATION_DB_URL" DB_USER="\$NOTIFICATION_DB_USER" 
  DB_PASSWORD="\$NOTIFICATION_DB_PASSWORD" \$JAVA -Xmx256m -jar medihelp-notific
  ation-service/target/medihelp-notification-service-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar &> 
  /tmp/notification.log &
  echo "  Notification PID: \$!"

  echo "[4/4] Waiting (50s)..."
  sleep 50

  echo ""
  echo "========================================="
  echo "  Service Health Check"
  echo "========================================="
  declare -A services=([8761]="Eureka" [8080]="Gateway" [8081]="Auth" 
  [8082]="User" [8083]="Health" [8084]="Prescription" [8085]="Notification")
  for port in 8761 8080 8081 8082 8083 8084 8085; do
      status=\$(curl -s -o /dev/null -w "%{http_code}" 
  http://localhost:\$port/actuator/health 2>/dev/null)
      name=\${services[\$port]}
      if [ "\$status" = "200" ]; then echo "  ✓ \$name (\$port): UP"; else echo 
  "  ✗ \$name (\$port): DOWN"; fi
  done
  SCRIPTEOF
  chmod +x ~/medihelp-src/deploy/scripts/start-all.sh
  echo "Script updated with full java path: $JAVA_CMD"

  Now restart:

  bash ~/medihelp-src/deploy/scripts/stop-all.sh

● The env + $JAVA approach still breaks because of how the shell parses the
  line. Let me take a completely different approach — export DB_URL before each 
  java command in separate subshells.

  Stop everything first:

  bash ~/medihelp-src/deploy/scripts/stop-all.sh

  Now write a clean script that avoids the inline env var problem entirely:

  cat > ~/medihelp-src/deploy/scripts/start-all.sh << 'EOF'
  #!/bin/bash
  PROJECT_DIR="${1:-$(dirname $(dirname $(dirname $(realpath $0))))}"
  cd "$PROJECT_DIR" || exit 1

  set -a; source "$PROJECT_DIR/.env" 2>/dev/null; set +a

  echo "========================================="
  echo "  MediHelp - Starting All Services"
  echo "========================================="

  echo "[1/4] Starting infrastructure..."
  docker compose -f docker-compose.infra.yml up -d 2>/dev/null
  sleep 5
  echo "  Infrastructure started."

  echo "[2/4] Starting Eureka..."
  java -Xmx192m -jar medihelp-eureka/target/medihelp-eureka-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar
  &> /tmp/eureka.log &
  echo "  PID: $!"
  for i in {1..40}; do curl -s http://localhost:8761/actuator/health | grep -q
  "UP" 2>/dev/null && echo "  Eureka is UP." && break; sleep 2; done

  echo "[3/4] Starting services..."
  java -Xmx192m -jar medihelp-gateway/target/medihelp-gateway-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar
   &> /tmp/gateway.log &
  echo "  Gateway PID: $!"

  (export DB_URL="$AUTH_DB_URL" DB_USER="$AUTH_DB_USER"
  DB_PASSWORD="$AUTH_DB_PASSWORD"; java -Xmx256m -jar
  medihelp-auth-service/target/medihelp-auth-service-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar) &>
  /tmp/auth.log &
  echo "  Auth PID: $!"

  (export DB_URL="$USER_DB_URL" DB_USER="$USER_DB_USER"
  DB_PASSWORD="$USER_DB_PASSWORD"; java -Xmx256m -jar
  medihelp-user-service/target/medihelp-user-service-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar) &>
  /tmp/user.log &
  echo "  User PID: $!"

  (export DB_URL="$HEALTH_DB_URL" DB_USER="$HEALTH_DB_USER"
  DB_PASSWORD="$HEALTH_DB_PASSWORD"; java -Xmx256m -jar
  medihelp-health-service/target/medihelp-health-service-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar) &>
  /tmp/health.log &
  echo "  Health PID: $!"

  (export DB_URL="$PRESCRIPTION_DB_URL" DB_USER="$PRESCRIPTION_DB_USER"
  DB_PASSWORD="$PRESCRIPTION_DB_PASSWORD"; java -Xmx256m -jar medihelp-prescript
  ion-service/target/medihelp-prescription-service-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar) &>
  /tmp/prescription.log &
  echo "  Prescription PID: $!"

  (export DB_URL="$NOTIFICATION_DB_URL" DB_USER="$NOTIFICATION_DB_USER"
  DB_PASSWORD="$NOTIFICATION_DB_PASSWORD"; java -Xmx256m -jar medihelp-notificat
  ion-service/target/medihelp-notification-service-1.0.0-SNAPSHOT.jar) &>
  /tmp/notification.log &
  echo "  Notification PID: $!"

  echo "[4/4] Waiting (50s)..."
  sleep 50

  echo ""
  echo "========================================="
  echo "  Service Health Check"
  echo "========================================="
  declare -A services=([8761]="Eureka" [8080]="Gateway" [8081]="Auth"
  [8082]="User" [8083]="Health" [8084]="Prescription" [8085]="Notification")
  for port in 8761 8080 8081 8082 8083 8084 8085; do
      status=$(curl -s -o /dev/null -w "%{http_code}"
  http://localhost:$port/actuator/health 2>/dev/null)
      name=${services[$port]}
      if [ "$status" = "200" ]; then echo "  ✓ $name ($port): UP"; else echo "  
  ✗ $name ($port): DOWN"; fi
  done
  EOF
  chmod +x ~/medihelp-src/deploy/scripts/start-all.sh
  echo "Script ready"

  Now start:

  bash ~/medihelp-src/deploy/scripts/start-all.sh

  This uses subshells (export ...; java ...) which guarantees each service gets
  its own DB_URL. Share the health check output.

Install Grafana Alloy                                                           
Before you configure this integration, you must set up Grafana Alloy.           
Grafana Alloy is a component-based telemetry collector. It focuses on ease of   
use, adaptability to your needs, and easy debugging. You configure Grafana      
Alloy with Alloy Configuration Syntax, an HCL-inspired expression language that 
 uses small reusable blocks that work together to form programmable pipelines.  
                                                                                
Read more about Grafana Alloy                                                   
                                                                                
Run Grafana Alloy

token will appear as the password in the configuration below.

● Got it. Now SSH into the Azure VM and set up Alloy. Run these one by one:

  Step 1: Install Grafana Alloy

  sudo apt-get install -y gpg && wget -q -O - https://apt.grafana.com/gpg.key |
  gpg --dearmor | sudo tee /etc/apt/keyrings/grafana.gpg > /dev/null && echo
  "deb [signed-by=/etc/apt/keyrings/grafana.gpg] https://apt.grafana.com stable 
  main" | sudo tee /etc/apt/sources.list.d/grafana.list && sudo apt-get update
  && sudo apt-get install -y alloy

  Step 2: Write the config

  sudo tee /etc/alloy/config.alloy << 'EOF'
  // Scrape all MediHelp services
  prometheus.scrape "medihelp_services" {
    targets = [
      {"__address__" = "localhost:8761", "service" = "eureka"},
      {"__address__" = "localhost:8080", "service" = "gateway"},
      {"__address__" = "localhost:8081", "service" = "auth"},
      {"__address__" = "localhost:8082", "service" = "user"},
      {"__address__" = "localhost:8083", "service" = "health"},
      {"__address__" = "localhost:8084", "service" = "prescription"},
      {"__address__" = "localhost:8085", "service" = "notification"},
    ]
    metrics_path = "/actuator/prometheus"
    scrape_interval = "30s"
    forward_to = [prometheus.remote_write.grafana_cloud.receiver]
  }

  prometheus.remote_write "grafana_cloud" {
    endpoint {
      url =
  "https://prometheus-prod-43-prod-ap-south-1.grafana.net/api/prom/push"
      basic_auth {
        username = "3092790"
        password = "glc_eyJvIjoiMTcyMjM4NyIsIm4iOiJzdGFjay0xNTg0MjgxLWFsbG95LW1l
  ZGloZWxwLWFsbG95IiwiayI6Illyd3A5VDVuMTFwUjY5WjE5ODBRbEpWWiIsIm0iOnsiciI6InByb2
  QtYXAtc291dGgtMSJ9fQ=="
      }
    }
  }
  EOF

  Step 3: Start Alloy

  sudo systemctl restart alloy && sudo systemctl enable alloy && sudo systemctl
  status alloy | head -5

  prometheus.scrape "medihelp" {

      {"__address__" = "localhost:8761", "service" = "eureka"},
      {"__address__" = "localhost:8080", "service" = "gateway"},

Unique identifier (UID)                                                         
The unique identifier (UID) of a dashboard can be used to uniquely identify a   
dashboard between multiple Grafana installs. The UID allows having consistent   
URLs for accessing dashboards so changing the title of a dashboard will not     
break any bookmarked links to that dashboard.

● It's showing data! Now let's build a complete MediHelp monitoring dashboard.
  Stay on that dashboard and add more panels:

  Panel 1 (the one you just created): Change the title to Heap Memory by Service
   by clicking the panel title → Edit → change title at the right side → Apply.

  Panel 2: Click Add → Visualization → query:
  process_cpu_usage * 100
  Title: CPU Usage (%) → Apply

  Panel 3: Click Add → Visualization → query:
  up
  Change visualization type (top right) to Stat → Title: Service Status → Apply

  Panel 4: Click Add → Visualization → query:
  http_server_requests_seconds_count
  Title: HTTP Request Count → Apply

  Panel 5: Click Add → Visualization → query:
  sum(jvm_threads_live_threads) by (application)
  Title: Live Threads → Apply

  Panel 6: Click Add → Visualization → query:
  sum(jvm_memory_used_bytes{area="nonheap"}) by (application)
  Title: Non-Heap Memory → Apply

  After adding all panels, click the save icon (💾) at the top → name it
  MediHelp Monitoring → Save.

  Your Grafana monitoring URL will be: subhrajitd28.grafana.net

  your project demo!
